<div id="review_175893517" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/175893517" />
    <a title="Walt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1005462-walt"><img alt="Walt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1235589111p2/1005462.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/175893517?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Walt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Walt" href="/user/show/1005462-walt">Walt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10955104-please-look-after-mom">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer175893517" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15870370774923638971">Piercing.<br/><br/>This novel about a Korean family cut and passed through me, stabbing me, penetrating my soul.<br/><br/>Yeah, that's the adjective I want to use, piercing. That word describes my thoughts about PLEASE LOOK AFTER MOM by Kyung-sook Shin.<br/><br/>The novel's story, which recounts interactions and their resulting implications between a husband and his wife and the same with respect to a daughter and son from the same family with their beloved mother, made its way through me. It forced its way into my conscienc</span>
  <span id="freeText15870370774923638971" style="display:none">Piercing.<br /><br />This novel about a Korean family cut and passed through me, stabbing me, penetrating my soul.<br /><br />Yeah, that's the adjective I want to use, piercing. That word describes my thoughts about PLEASE LOOK AFTER MOM by Kyung-sook Shin.<br /><br />The novel's story, which recounts interactions and their resulting implications between a husband and his wife and the same with respect to a daughter and son from the same family with their beloved mother, made its way through me. It forced its way into my conscience as a son, as a husband, and as a father. I could identify with its characters and their flaws and failings in many ways, even though it was set in a foreign land with people of a different race and milieu than mine. It moved me deeply relative to its characters and story, but at the same time, it made me introspective as to my roles in similar situations in America. Also, it's foreign setting provided entertaining novelties --- for example, ancestral rites, various food dishes and historical sites, and the Full Moon Harvest --- I was unfamiliar with and interested in learning and hearing about.<br /><br />However, in using "piercing" here, I realize the nature of the word has changed during the later years in my life up until now.<br /><br />I'm in my sixties, and the way the word "piercing" is used today is different than it was when I was younger. The word "piercing" now has a meaning that predominates in contemporary culture that it didn't have when I was younger, one that doesn't seem nearly as poignant as that older meaning. "Piercing" now often refers to the accommodation for a decoration and/or a modification to a body, usually a person's body. It can include, for instance, tattooing and the making holes to accommodate ear and nose rings and the like. It relates, as I understand it, to body art. So when I use piercing here, I use it in the earlier sense.<br /><br />I liked how Kyung-sook Shin utilized varying points of view in her depiction of characters' reactions to Mom gone missing. I also liked how the author utilized the less familiar second person in telling the Father's and daughter's stories. I also liked the subtle underlay of faith and its final manifestation in the story arc.<br /><br />After reading the book, I feel it has touched me and informed me, made my life more interesting and me more introspective because it has cut and passed through me, stabbed me, and penetrated my soul perhaps in a way that younger persons may feel informed by various manifestations of body art they undergo, including piercings and tattoos.<br /><br />Piercing.<br /><br />I wrote Time for All Eternity.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15870370774923638971" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2284408882746929916"><i> From BBC Radio 4: </i><br/><br/>Please Look After Mother tells the story of So-nyo, an elderly wife and mother, who goes missing on Seoul station.   <span id="freeText2284408882746929916" style="display:none"><i> From BBC Radio 4: </i><br /><br />Please Look After Mother tells the story of So-nyo, an elderly wife and mother, who goes missing on Seoul station. Only with her gone, do her children and her husband begin to appreciate not only all she has done for them, but who she really was. As first her daughter, then her son and then her husband search the streets for her, we learn, too, how much they have left unsaid.<br /><br />A story in part about the cultural clash between the generation who inhabit modern, urban Seoul and their parents steeped in the rural traditions of Korea, Please Look After Mother is also a universal and humbling reminder of how easy it is to take the people we love for granted.</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7077482030344130907">"Please Look After Mom" is about a remarkable woman who is virtually invisible to her husband and adult children until she disappears one day in a Seoul subway station. Her absence allows them to see and appreciate her for the first time. This powerful novel about motherhood resonated in a very personal way for me - both as a daughter and mother. </span>

<div id="review_2430741405" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2430741405" />
    <a title="Renita D&#39;Silva" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17336261-renita-d-silva"><img alt="Renita D&#39;Silva" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442881639p2/17336261.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Renita D&#39;Silva" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Renita D&#39;Silva" href="/user/show/17336261-renita-d-silva">Renita D&#39;Silva</a>

<div id="review_1006025599" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1006025599" />
    <a title="Homa Sharifmousavi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3729067-homa-sharifmousavi"><img alt="Homa Sharifmousavi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1526598424p2/3729067.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1006025599?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Homa Sharifmousavi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Homa Sharifmousavi" href="/user/show/3729067-homa-sharifmousavi">Homa Sharifmousavi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20124221-please-look-after-mom">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3729067-homa-sharifmousavi?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1006025599" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10798497421824024651">The setting of the story is in Korea,the countryside where an old couple live and Seoul where their children live.Story starts with their mom missing because she accidentally parted from her husband on the trip they took to Seoul to celebrate their birthdays with their children.As the story goes we start to find out more about Mom and her relationship with her family members and we find out she was suffering from some kind of dementia that made it hard for her to find her way in the city.Each ch</span>
  <span id="freeText10798497421824024651" style="display:none">The setting of the story is in Korea,the countryside where an old couple live and Seoul where their children live.Story starts with their mom missing because she accidentally parted from her husband on the trip they took to Seoul to celebrate their birthdays with their children.As the story goes we start to find out more about Mom and her relationship with her family members and we find out she was suffering from some kind of dementia that made it hard for her to find her way in the city.Each chapter is told from one person's point of view,oldest daughter,oldest son,father and mom herself.Through their memories and thoughts we begin to understand more about their life,about how mom lived,how she got sick and how little her family knew her. <br />In two chapters the author uses second-person narrative which I think it's very hard and rare but works perfectly in this book.The second person narrative makes you relate even more to the story,it makes you feel the pain and feelings of the characters more.It's more intimate than the third person narrative in other chapters.It's like their memories are yours,like it's your mom that is missing.<br />It's only when mom is narrating the story that you understand how lonely she was and how none of her family members knew her.they didn't know her as a person,only as mom,as wife.throughout the book every one calls her mom,wife or sister in law.she's never mentioned by her name until the part when she is talking about a friend,that friend is the only one who says her name "Park So-nyo". Only her friend,the man who helped her bury her dead newborn,called her by name several times.<br />when I was reading this part I wondered if she loved this man,if she loved her husband and after that I wondered if my mom loved my dad,if my grandmother loved my grandfather.<br />Although mom did everything for her family she still felt guilty,she always said I'm sorry to her children,I wonder do all mothers feel that guilty?the way she feels guilty makes me angry.I'm angry with her and I'm angry with her children and her husband.(and I think I'm even a little angry with myself)<br />It's the kind of a story that everyone can relate to,I don't think anyone would hate it but some people might be bored with it because the writing is kind of slow in some parts.<br />I'm still thinking about it after reading,I have so many vivid pictures of their memories,of their home in my mind.the more you think about it the more you find out about other aspects of the story.<br />Parts of the book that I liked most are in my status updates.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10798497421824024651" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_167586760" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167586760" />
    <a title="Gaby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1185483-gaby"><img alt="Gaby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1241703457p2/1185483.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167586760?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gaby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gaby" href="/user/show/1185483-gaby">Gaby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1185483-gaby?shelf=multicultural">multicultural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1185483-gaby?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1185483-gaby?shelf=must-read">must-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167586760" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11064687546488918999">I'd read a review of Please Look After Mom in the New York Times. I was very excited to read and review the book when offered the chance through the Amazon Vine program. Written by one of South Korea's most widely read and highly respected authors, this is her first book translated into English.<br/><br/>Please Look After Mom tells the story of Park So-nyo, an elderly mother of five and grandmother, who gets separated from her husband in the subway at Seoul. Her husband and children begin a systematic sea</span>
  <span id="freeText11064687546488918999" style="display:none">I'd read a review of Please Look After Mom in the New York Times. I was very excited to read and review the book when offered the chance through the Amazon Vine program. Written by one of South Korea's most widely read and highly respected authors, this is her first book translated into English.<br /><br />Please Look After Mom tells the story of Park So-nyo, an elderly mother of five and grandmother, who gets separated from her husband in the subway at Seoul. Her husband and children begin a systematic search for her and as they do so, they realize that things have not been well with their mother for some time now. <br /><br />Shin tells the story from four perspectives: daughter, son, husband and wife. Each reveals aspects of Park So-nyo's life and her family life. The emotions that the story invokes goes beyond cultural lines: helplessness, desperation, shame, admiration, guilt, regret, and deep respect. Other reviewers have mentioned how Park So-nyo's story made them think of their lives and I echo this response, reading the book has me examining the close relationships in my life. <br /><br />Please Look After Mom is an amazing read and one of the best books that I've read in a long time. While on the surface it is a story about an older South Korean woman, it is really a story about love, parenthood, sacrifice, and family. It's message is universal - read the book and share it with people that you love.<br /><br />ISBN-10: 9780307593917 - Hardcover $24.95<br />Publisher: Knopf (April 5, 2011), 256 pages. <br />Review copy courtesy of the publisher and Amazon Vine. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11064687546488918999" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_145653449" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/145653449" />
    <a title="Jackie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1147841-jackie"><img alt="Jackie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1240450765p2/1147841.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/145653449?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jackie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jackie" href="/user/show/1147841-jackie">Jackie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1147841-jackie?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1147841-jackie?shelf=work-review-related-reading">work-review-related-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1147841-jackie?shelf=pleasure-reading">pleasure-reading</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer145653449" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5185615493886229922">Kyung-sook Shin is a best selling Korean author who is finally in <br/>translation here in the States. And, oh my, how glad I am. Her <br/>writing is mesmerizing, deep and beautiful. She pushes the reader <br/>into the story by literally using referring to "you" as the narrating <br/>character. "You" are looking for your 69 year old mother who <br/>disappeared in a Seoul subway station on the way to a birthday dinner. <br/>Sometimes "you" are the oldest daughter, other times "you" are the <br/>favored son. Sometimes you are looki</span>
  <span id="freeText5185615493886229922" style="display:none">Kyung-sook Shin is a best selling Korean author who is finally in <br />translation here in the States. And, oh my, how glad I am. Her <br />writing is mesmerizing, deep and beautiful. She pushes the reader <br />into the story by literally using referring to "you" as the narrating <br />character. "You" are looking for your 69 year old mother who <br />disappeared in a Seoul subway station on the way to a birthday dinner. <br />Sometimes "you" are the oldest daughter, other times "you" are the <br />favored son. Sometimes you are looking through the lives and memory <br />of the negligent husband, sometimes "you" are the ever-working but <br />never appreciated mother of the family. The intensity of this way of <br />story telling is heart-breaking and addictive--putting this book down <br />is almost impossible. Keep some tissues handy, and make sure you have <br />a free evening, then dive into this book and ride the emotional tidal <br />wave--you will close the book exhausted but grateful for the journey.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5185615493886229922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qgS27QGQXZFX0E0MNH0Hrqi33WOy0BeAwipRVvgnjVgqSHgeOv2SHDorMutYEqiYpRX4n7VZaFgHWuPgl3X6ug==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OMLRfts/DmkVuK2eWE2s1fGIr/xn3vRi2Tg5bIn2XhG4jh+N4FLB5HhD0nk0IgPj/CqKAGBXi7ocSIva5qQp8w==')})
  }

프로그램에<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText7411349205328097771\" style=\"display:none\">“사람들이 나보고 맘충이래.” 한국에서 여자로 살아가는 일 그 공포, 피로, 당황, 놀람, 혼란, 좌절의 연속에 대한 인생 현장 보고서 조남주 장편소설 『82년생 김지영』이 민음사 ‘오늘의 젊은 작가’ 시리즈로 출간되었다. 조남주 작가는 2011년, 지적 장애가 있는 한 소년의 재능이 발견되면서 벌어지는 사건을 통해 삶의 부조리를 현실적이면서도 따뜻하게 그려낸 작품 『귀를 귀울이면』으로 ‘문학동네소설상’을 받으며 데뷔했다. 시사 교양 프로그램에서 10년 동안 일한 방송 작가답게 서민들의 일상에서 발생하는 비극을 사실적이고 공감대 높은 스토리로 표현하는 데 특출 난 재능을 보이는 작가는 신작 『82년생 김지영』에서 30대를 살고 있는 한국 여성들의 보편적인 일상을 완벽하게 재현한다. 주인공 ‘김지영 씨’의 기억을 바탕으로 한 고백을 한 축으로, 고백을 뒷받침하는 각종 통계 자료와 기사들을 또 다른 축으로 삼는 이 소설은 1982년생 김지영 씨로 대변되는 ‘그녀’들의 인생 마디마디에 존재하는 성차별적 요소를 핍진하게 묘사한다. 이를 통해 작가는 제도적 성차별이 줄어든 시대의 보이지 않는 차별들이 어떻게 여성들의 삶을 제약하고 억압하는지 보여 준다. 여권이 신장된 시대, 그러나 여전히 ‘여성’이라는 조건이 굴레로 존재하는 사회에서 살아가는 한 여자의 인생을 다룬 『82년생 김지영』은 조용한 고백과 뜨거운 고발로 완성된 새로운 페미니즘 소설이자 수많은 사람들의 경험과 자료로 이루어진 ‘목소리 소설’이다. 맘충이, 여혐, 메갈리아 등 연일 새롭게 등장하는 페미니즘 화두를 관심 있게 지켜보는 독자라면 누구나 흥미롭게 읽을 수 있고 저마다 의미를 발견할 수 있을 것이다<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"7411349205328097771\" href=\"#\" Though she is repulsed by his crimes, something about the depth of his suffering strikes a chord in her. Shaken by their encounter, she returns to visit him the next week. In doing so they form a deep, unbreakable bond, helping one another overcome their demons. Bà không hề biết, con gái bà thực sự muốn trở thành nhà văn hơn cả...\n\nCác bậc phụ huynh cứ hi vọng và cả áp đặt rằng con sẽ trở thành thế này thế kia mà quên mất rằng họ nên nhìn nhận con cái mình là chính-bản-thân-chúng và để con cái được lớn lên trở thành người mà chính-chúng-là.\n\nKanae Minato, nữ nhà văn nổi tiếng Nhật Bản, với lối khắc họa tâm lý nhân vật trong các tác phẩm khai thác góc khuất ẩn sâu của tâm lý con người... sẽ khiến bạn đi từ bất ngờ này đến bất ngờ khác sau những khoảnh khắc bạn bế tắc, hoang mang, cô đơn... giống như từng nhân vật trong cuốn sách.       <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/13443181">Quotes from Please Look After...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;You realize that you habitually thought of Mom when something in your life was not going well, because when you thought of her it was as though something got back on track, and you felt re-energized.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/445129-you-realize-that-you-habitually-thought-of-mom-when-something">168 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;...I have so many dreams of my own, and I remember things from my childhood, from when I was a girl and a young woman, and I haven't forgotten a thing. So why did we think of Mom as a mom from the very beginning? She didn't have the opportunity to pursue her dreams, and all by herself, faced everything the era dealt her, poverty and sadness, and she couldn't do anything about her very bad lot in life other than suffer through it and get beyond it and live her life to the very best of her ability, giving her body and her heart to it completely. Why did I never give a thought to Mom's dreams?&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/445122-i-have-so-many-dreams-of-my-own-and-i">147 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
